    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/130892-if-you-only-had-a-year-to-live-what-would">If you only had a year to live, what would you do?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_130892'><a id="like_count_community_question_130892" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/130892?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F21795840-a-time-to-die">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/130892-if-you-only-had-a-year-to-live-what-would">6 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/130892-if-you-only-had-a-year-to-live-what-would">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/25035684-nadine-brandes"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1484497507i/25035684._UX100_CR0,24,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/25035684-nadine-brandes">Nadine Brandes</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I pulled some of these answers from <a href='http://nadinebrandes.com/2014/09/03/if-i-had-one-year-left-to-live-a-time-to-die-blog-tour/' rel='nofollow noopener'>a blog post</a> I wrote on the topic, only because I felt that it was already answered succinctly. :-)<br/><br/>If I felt God wa<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I pulled some of these answers from <a href="http://nadinebrandes.com/2014/09/03/if-i-had-one-year-left-to-live-a-time-to-die-blog-tour/" rel="nofollow noopener">a blog post</a> I wrote on the topic, only because I felt that it was already answered succinctly. :-)<br /><br />If I felt God was giving the "ok", I would commit some hard-core writing months (about three or four) to completing the Out of Time series. For the sake of my readers (yes, for you!) If I couldn’t finish it in that time, I’d start looking for authors who could finish it/polish it for me.<br /><br />I would write intentional letters.<br />Words are my passion. I would make sure I had a stack of letters to be given to each person I love after I passed on, hopefully encouraging them to pursue life and God full-speed and to REJOICE at my joining Christ in heaven.<br /><br />I would visit my relatives.<br />I grew up away from most of my relatives so I didn’t build the relationships with some of them that I would have liked. I would take at least two weeks to a month and road trip (with the hubby, of course!) around America, visiting them, having intentional quality time with them, and — with some — trying one last time to share the importance of Christ.<br /><br />I would pray and fast more.<br />This is one of those things I already try to do, but I’m a spiritual wimp. Praying is the more tough side of relationship with Christ for me. I would love to devote hours — and I mean carpetburns-on-the-knees hours — to praying, fasting, and communing with God. The one time I intentionally fasted and pushed myself past my human desires, it completely changed me. And that was just one time.<br /><br />I would tell my story.<br />This one would take the most courage. There are very few people who know my full life story, but recently God’s been urging me to share it — the nitty gritty, the mistakes, the spiritual doubts…all of it. But it’s hard to completely bare our souls to others, especially if we’re expecting disapproval.<br /><br />So…I would suck it up and either start telling my story (verbally) or through book-form. I already know God can use it to touch many other lives. I just need to push through my own insecurities and trust Him in my weakness.<br /><br />Some little things:<br />I would go skydiving, sleep on an overnight train (preferably the Trans-Siberian Rail, which — if I go to Russia — would be very doable.), ride a tandem bike, and send up a desperate plea to J K Rowling (who probably won’t even see it) asking her to let me treat her to a cup of tea.<br /><br />But, these are little things. Inconsequential things. Not big enough to be labeled as dreams, they’re just desires that would provide me with temporary happiness and then a good story.<br /> <br /><br />My real goal in my last year would be to live as passionately as my weak, shy, cowardly human body allows for God’s glory.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1087868100?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadine Brandes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadine Brandes" href="/user/show/25035684-nadine-brandes">Nadine Brandes</a>

          added it

      <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://nadinebrandes.com/blog/">http://nadinebrandes.com/blog/</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1087868100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18209744323835434482">I'm certainly not going to write a review for my own book. That kind of defeats the purpose of reviews. BUT...I thought I'd include a parental guide for those who like to know exactly what type of content is going to be in the book.<br/><br/><b>PARENT'S GUIDE</b><br/><br/>I recommend this book for ages 14 and up, though the maturity of the reader plays a big part. So, basically, if you're a parent...know your child's reading level.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Profanity:</i>
</b> NONE<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Intimacy: </i>
</b> There is attraction between a boy and girl, but no kissing</span>
  <span id="freeText18209744323835434482" style="display:none">I'm certainly not going to write a review for my own book. That kind of defeats the purpose of reviews. BUT...I thought I'd include a parental guide for those who like to know exactly what type of content is going to be in the book.<br /><br /><b>PARENT'S GUIDE</b><br /><br />I recommend this book for ages 14 and up, though the maturity of the reader plays a big part. So, basically, if you're a parent...know your child's reading level.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Profanity:</i>
</b> NONE<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Intimacy: </i>
</b> There is attraction between a boy and girl, but no kissing.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Violence:</i>
</b> This is where I advise parents to use the most caution. There is violence in this book (details below), but it doesn't get graphic. However, the scenes can certainly be disturbing to some readers. Click on "spoiler" to see the scenes in detail:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[- A character gets her hand cut off. This is non-graphic, but the scene of trying to escape it is intense.<br />- Multiple characters die. These are major characters, so the scenes are emotional. One character is killed with an electronic chip in his brain. Another is shot. Again, non-graphic, but emotionally-heavy.<br />- A character gets shot in the arm.<br />- Another character has his arm amputated. Very non-graphic, but intense emotionally. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Scary scenes:</i>
</b> These scenes may not be <i>violent</i> but they can be scary. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[- Parvin fights wolves. She survives and escapes them, but...I just think wolves are scary. LOL.<br />- A character falls a long way, wielding a gun, and almost dies.<br />- There is a time when characters are battling a flash flood and almost drown.<br />- A character is resuscitated (successfully, yay!) but the moment can cause a little nervousness.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />Readers, if I've forgotten anything, please say so in the comments and I'll include it in here. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="18209744323835434482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1601178667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1601178667" />
    <a title="Madelyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38028659-madelyn"><img alt="Madelyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534850487p2/38028659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1601178667?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madelyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madelyn" href="/user/show/38028659-madelyn">Madelyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38028659-madelyn?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38028659-madelyn?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1601178667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11237997332354727340">FULL REVIEW HERE: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://literarycafe.weebly.com/home/a-time-to-die-out-of-time-1-nadine-brandes'>http://literarycafe.weebly.com/home/a...</a><br/><br/>I finished this book approximately three weeks ago. It has taken me the entirety of that time to gather my incoherent fangirling thoughts and write this whirlwind of a review. <br/><br/>I'm sure <b>everyone</b> has a book that they can't stop seeing around. Wherever you go, wherever you look, it somehow always seems to pop up. For me, that was this book. Why I ignored it for so long I still do not know (Especially with that gorgeous cover. Ask anyone. I'm</span>
  <span id="freeText11237997332354727340" style="display:none">FULL REVIEW HERE: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://literarycafe.weebly.com/home/a-time-to-die-out-of-time-1-nadine-brandes">http://literarycafe.weebly.com/home/a...</a><br><br>I finished this book approximately three weeks ago. It has taken me the entirety of that time to gather my incoherent fangirling thoughts and write this whirlwind of a review. <br><br>I'm sure <b>everyone</b> has a book that they can't stop seeing around. Wherever you go, wherever you look, it somehow always seems to pop up. For me, that was this book. Why I ignored it for so long I still do not know (Especially with that gorgeous cover. Ask anyone. I'm all about the covers). <br><br>I suppose you could say this was my most anticipate book of the year. I, for some reason, am always hesitant to start them. I assume it's because I've built up such high expectations, and more often than not, they disappoint. I am happy to say this one lived up to my hopes and dreams, even more.<br> <br>"Enjoy the little things in life," they say. One of my very favorite 'little things' happens to be quotes. So, without further ado, we begin:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471378478i/20040331._SX540_.jpg" width="800" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> "I enter my room and shut the door softly, like a whisper. If I could unbutton my soul and hang it up, it's downtrodden state might dry off by morning. Instead, I lie on my bed and let it float in my emotions."<br><br>"Mere survival holds no purpose. I refuse to believe God created us to just get by, so where does that put me?"<br><br>​"I can't comprehend the full emotion in his wrinkled brow and grinding jaw, but his eyes hold deeper sorrow than I've ever witnessed in my short life. In this moment, I realize how very different sorrow is from pity."</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471377120i/20040175.jpg" width="600" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <br>Generally, I create a long list full of specific things I enjoyed from a book (like plot, character details, resolve, etc). I'm going to change it up today and make it special because this, my friends, is a very special book. I'm going to create a few different categories and list my favorites from them under that. Sorry if that was confusing. You'll soon figure it out.<br><br> <i>
  <b>Technology</b>
</i><br><br>This novel (partly because it was a sci-fi) is filled with brilliant new technology. While it's hard to choose, let me introduce you to the three objects of my highest esteem:<br><br><b>-CLOTHING:</b><br>I will just say, the suits Parvin tests out are the epitome of every little kid's 'being a spy' dream.<br><b>-SENTRA:</b><br>By the end of the book, I was head over heels in love with this idea. For those of you who haven't read the book, a sentra can be described as a small device which (by pricking your finger, wrist, neck, etc.) uses your blood to take a 'picture' of your emotion at that moment. Then by the same method, someone else can take the chip the sentra produces and feel your emotion for several seconds, as well as your fleeting thoughts. Don't you want one now?<br><b>-MUSIC CHIP:</b><br>​I'm pretty sure when I say that every teenager in the modern world would want one of these, that I'm correct. A music chip is exactly what it sounds like. A chip inserted into your bloodstream which monitors your emotions and plays music to go along with your feelings. Need I say more? I think not. <br><br> <i>
  <b>World:</b>
</i><br><br><b>-TIGHTROPE SOCIETY:</b><br>​One day several months ago I was contemplating the possibility of a race/species that had perfect balance who lived in treehouses and walked from house to house with tightropes... But Nadine made it even better by having a civilization with advanced technology operate on them. Wow. <br><br> <i>
  <b>Characters:</b>
</i><br><br><b>-SOLOMON:</b><br>​I know. He plays a small part. But I have a feeling that will change in the next book, and I want to go on record saying that I like him before he does something utterly heroic and steals all of our hearts. But maybe I'm wrong because I have received many warnings from fellow fangirls (who, by the way, fangirl Jude, not Solomon *cough*- hann, amanda, hannah *cough*). Who knows? <br><b>-SKELLY CHASE:</b><br>​I took a test to see which character's personality I was most similar to, and I just so happened to wind up with Skelly Chase. True Story. (you can take the test here:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.playbuzz.com/nadine10/which-a-time-to-die-character-are-you?utm_source=pinterest.com&amp;utm_medium=ff&amp;utm_campaign=ff">http://www.playbuzz.com/nadine10/whic...</a>). Even though he's the villain, I did enjoy how Nadine crafted him.<br> <br><i>
  <b>Names:</b>
</i><br><br><b>-ELM, WILLOW, ASH:</b><br>From the Albino society, these were my very favorite names. So creative. Plus they fit their personalities, in my opinion. <br><b>-PARVIN:</b><br>​Initially, I had second guesses about this name. It's incredibly unique, and I don't believe I've ever heard it before. But as I neared the end and had become used to it, I began to appreciate how uncommon it was. For me, it was perfect because she's such a one-of-a-kind person, she deserved a one-of-a-kind name. <br><br>There you have it! I hope I wasn't too squealy​. But truly, this is now in my top favorite books list (of which there are only two. Including this one.) <br><br>Full review (with even more pictures :D) here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://literarycafe.weebly.com/home/a-time-to-die-out-of-time-1-nadine-brandes">http://literarycafe.weebly.com/home/a...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11237997332354727340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2229496219" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2229496219" />
    <a title="Sarah Grace Grzy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy"><img alt="Sarah Grace Grzy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570047933p2/59507807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2229496219?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Grace Grzy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Grace Grzy" href="/user/show/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy">Sarah Grace Grzy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Ages 16+ violence</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=want-to-own">want-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=indie">indie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2229496219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6663046103327587951">Wow. Wow. Wow. I just don't even know how to review this . . . but I'll do my best. <br/><br/>This book is so incredibly *deep* it almost made my brain hurt sometimes. Brandes tackles some very good - and weighty - questions throughout, and handles them in an exceptional manner. It really makes you think - which I loved. Some of the concepts and ideas just blew my mind. <br/><br/>The characters were a ton of fun, not to mentioned relatable, honest, and real. The MC, Parvin, is just like any one of us. She wants to </span>
  <span id="freeText6663046103327587951" style="display:none">Wow. Wow. Wow. I just don't even know how to review this . . . but I'll do my best. <br /><br />This book is so incredibly *deep* it almost made my brain hurt sometimes. Brandes tackles some very good - and weighty - questions throughout, and handles them in an exceptional manner. It really makes you think - which I loved. Some of the concepts and ideas just blew my mind. <br /><br />The characters were a ton of fun, not to mentioned relatable, honest, and real. The MC, Parvin, is just like any one of us. She wants to do the right thing, she wants to be selfless. She wants to trust God and have faith. But yet she's scared to death, and questions God when everything seems to be going wrong. She's human. She struggles with the same exact issues that I do, and you do. Not to mention her sarcasm was pretty awesome. XD Her character arc was masterfully done, and I knew within only a few chapters that Brandes is an incredibly talented author. <br />Other characters such as Jude, Hawke, Reid and Willow, were also fantastic. Jude's story particularly really caught my interest. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Although did he really have to die in the end?! Really!? Was is necessary to completely obliterate my heart within pages of the end?? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I wasn't really a fan of the romance between Jude and Parvin, and that's part of the reason I docked a star. <br />Hawke's character was pretty understated, but I know he will be far more prominent in future books, which I am really looking forward to. <br />Reid, though, was the very best. I may or may not have a brother-crush on that character. He was just the sweetest and reminded me in many ways of my own brothers. &lt;3 <br /><br />The story and setting was very fascinating. There were times were the plot lagged a bit, and I lost interest, but I am glad I pushed through, as it was totally worth it. There were some aspects that I found overly-creepy, such as the albino's lifestyle? What even? Just ew . . . That first scene in the albino village had me creeped out. That, and a few other aspects were too violent for my tastes, but that's entirely just my feelings on that matter. <br /><br />All in all, this book was really. really. well written. Just wow! As I said before, it is incredibly clear that Brandes is a talented author, and I look forward to reading more by her! <br /><br />Recommended for ages 16+ for violence and mild romance. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A character gets her hand amputated (as punishment), and another an arm. There are mentions of suicide and euthanasia. Also people being held at gunpoint, shot, being attacked, etc. Also some "creepy" elements that are part of the futuristic world.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="6663046103327587951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40760365-hannah-rodes?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40760365-hannah-rodes?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1422263772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1423942635331639902">A Time to Die by Nadine Brandes<br/> <br/> Parvin Brielle Blackwater is seventeen years old and has only one more year to live. Same as everyone else in the East side of the wall, Parvin has a clock counting down to the day she is going to die. When it is found out that Parvin has been illegally sharing a clock with her brother Reid, she is thrown over the wall—her peoples death sentence. Here she finds her calling and grows closer to God. But now with only six months to live, is it too late to except tha</span>
  <span id="freeText1423942635331639902" style="display:none">A Time to Die by Nadine Brandes<br /> <br /> Parvin Brielle Blackwater is seventeen years old and has only one more year to live. Same as everyone else in the East side of the wall, Parvin has a clock counting down to the day she is going to die. When it is found out that Parvin has been illegally sharing a clock with her brother Reid, she is thrown over the wall—her peoples death sentence. Here she finds her calling and grows closer to God. But now with only six months to live, is it too late to except that calling? <br /> <br /> Once again I fell in love with the beautiful characters Nadine Brandes crafted in her novel. I totally felt Parvin was relatable and I loved her more the second read through. I don’t know, I just loved everything more the second read through. Maybe because I actually slowed down and didn’t read it to quickly and process hardly anything, like my first read. *scowls at self* <br /><br /> My goodness. This was my second time reading A Time to Die and I caught so many more things. I just seriously, want to cuddle and cry, while I think about wiser ways to spend my time. A Time to Die totally inspired me to be all I can be for God, and I just am so happy I re-read this. You just need to read A Time to Die. It will be way, worth your precious time. <br /> <br /> (And I. Can’t. Resist. This. The. Temptation. Is. To. Strong.) Tally Ho! <br /></span>

<div id="review_1073570906" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1073570906" />
    <a title="Shantelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5482096-shantelle"><img alt="Shantelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471497290p2/5482096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1073570906?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shantelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shantelle" href="/user/show/5482096-shantelle">Shantelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=dystopian-sci-fi">dystopian-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=gruesome-violent">gruesome-violent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=on-my-bookshelf">on-my-bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1073570906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4652849471394581400">I recently came to love dystopian. It intrigues me. Thrills me. So when I saw that <i>A Time to Die</i> by Nadine Brandes was a Christian dystopian, I was so excited to read it! Now I sit here, contemplating. One star? Four stars? Five stars? It was raw, it was riveting, it was heart-<i>breaking</i>! I suppose I won't know exactly what I think about this book until I read the second book in the series. But no, no, the one star is out of the question. <i>A Time to Die</i> is a too well-written and fascinating of a ta</span>
  <span id="freeText4652849471394581400" style="display:none">I recently came to love dystopian. It intrigues me. Thrills me. So when I saw that <i>A Time to Die</i> by Nadine Brandes was a Christian dystopian, I was so excited to read it! Now I sit here, contemplating. One star? Four stars? Five stars? It was raw, it was riveting, it was heart-<i>breaking</i>! I suppose I won't know exactly what I think about this book until I read the second book in the series. But no, no, the one star is out of the question. <i>A Time to Die</i> is a too well-written and fascinating of a tale to get only one star! *smiles*<br /><br />Parvin Blackwater has one year left to live. And she's only eighteen. Her clock is slowly loosing its numbers, ticking ever closer to her death. But she has yet to really <i>live</i>! And she sees injustice and wrongs around her that she aches to fight against. Yet what difference can she make with so little time left?<br />Step into this broken, futuristic world and go on a wild journey with Parvin as she discovers things she has never before known.<br /><br />The dystopian aspect and world was amazing. Well thought-out. Terrible. Real. Absolutely intriguing. I saw a few similarities to <i>Divergent</i> and <i>The Hunger Games</i> pop up here and there ... yet <i>A Time to Die</i> was so very different than them even so. It's definitely its own unique dystopian world.<br /><br />I was surprised and startled again and again. Nadine Brandes had so many unexpected twists waiting around the corner! Wow. I was hooked, and finished this story in no time.<br /><br />The theme was awesome. It made me think: <i>What would I do if this was my last year?</i> It honestly scared me, because, like Parvin, I sometimes feel purposeless, useless ... like I've wasted my years so far. I can identify with her - that longing to leave a mark on the world. To make a difference for good. To live life to the fullest; to use what God has given you! ...But then, not knowing how. Not feeling like my efforts amount to anything. So yes. It was incredible to journey along with her and watch her grow. Poignant to feel her desperate emotions.<br />I also loved the whole theme with 'Shalom'. It was so very beautiful. So very deep. Every part of that was brilliant, and definitely makes a reader want to draw nearer to God. Beautiful job, Nadine! ^_^ Eep! I could go on about it, but I don't want to give any spoilers. Read <i>A Time to Die</i> and experience it for yourself, people!<br /><br />So yes. I identified with Parvin. Despite some slightly foolish choices, I really liked her character. She wasn't the hard, "fake", arrogant, kick-butt heroine that some dystopian (and fantasy and perhaps historical) novels like to display. Instead she was someone I could relate to; someone I could cheer on. Jude was hard er to understand sometimes, but I liked him too. And Solomon Hawke was sweet. Willow was a sweetie too. Oh my word, I just want to explode right now with anger at a certain person and a certain people group ... but I'll keep myself from doing so, so I want give away any spoilers! But be prepared to be angry. Very angry. This story stirs up emotions for sure. The sheer <i>injustice</i>!!! The betrayal! The absurdity! The hypocrisy! The way human life no longer holds its preciousness! O.O Grrr! It just made me so mad. <i>How could they?</i> And then try to pass it off as righteous or "just-the-way-it-is"?<br /><br />*Ahem* There was a bit of a budding romance going on; but nothing much. There was some violence. Definitely some gore. Nothing like reading <i>The Hunger Games</i>; but still sometimes I was left a bit squeamish or shocked.<br /><br />Overall, an absolutely gripping tale. And that ending! O.O I am so very happy that I will be reading <i>A Time to Speak</i> soon-ish here!<br /><br />If you like dystopian ... intricate mysteries ... wild journeys ... heart-pounding suspense ... tender moments ... themes of poignancy and depth ... Then you most certainly need to pick up <i>A Time to Die</i> and give it a try!<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of</i> A Time to Die <i>from the author in exchange for my honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4652849471394581400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1677007670" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1677007670" />
    <a title="Tracey Dyck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55528073-tracey-dyck"><img alt="Tracey Dyck" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579746018p2/55528073.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1677007670?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracey Dyck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracey Dyck" href="/user/show/55528073-tracey-dyck">Tracey Dyck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55528073-tracey-dyck?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55528073-tracey-dyck?shelf=realm-makers">realm-makers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55528073-tracey-dyck?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55528073-tracey-dyck?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55528073-tracey-dyck?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1677007670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1646887341081009973"><b>JANUARY 20/19 REVIEW</b><br/><br/>I still love it. My heart is still in pieces. I need book 2 ASAP—thank goodness it’s waiting on my shelf!<br/><br/><b>NOVEMBER 19/17 REVIEW </b><br/><br/>OH. MY. GOODNESS. This trilogy gets a lot of hype, at least in my reader circles, and I was desperately hoping it would live up to all those glowing reviews. IT DID. Bless Nadine's heart, it did.<br/><br/>This is one of the most unusual dystopian novels I've read, because it's infused with a lot more faith and hard questions and almost urban fantasy-ish setting</span>
  <span id="freeText1646887341081009973" style="display:none"><b>JANUARY 20/19 REVIEW</b><br /><br />I still love it. My heart is still in pieces. I need book 2 ASAP—thank goodness it’s waiting on my shelf!<br /><br /><b>NOVEMBER 19/17 REVIEW </b><br /><br />OH. MY. GOODNESS. This trilogy gets a lot of hype, at least in my reader circles, and I was desperately hoping it would live up to all those glowing reviews. IT DID. Bless Nadine's heart, it did.<br /><br />This is one of the most unusual dystopian novels I've read, because it's infused with a lot more faith and hard questions and almost urban fantasy-ish settings than others. One setting in particular almost felt out of place, but I found it so fascinating that I didn't care.<br /><br />But let's get back to the beginning. PARVIN. She is gold. I related to her so stinking much. In a society where everyone has a Clock counting down the time until they die, she has a year left and yearns to find her purpose, some way to make her last days count. She swings from apathy to passion a few times throughout the course of the novel, which was uncomfortably realistic (but in a good way). And she's something of a writer--well, technically an autobiographer--so that was neat.<br /><br /><b>Some quick thoughts on other characters:</b><br /><br />-Parvin's mom was hard to like at first, but that was on purpose, and I felt their somewhat rocky relationship was done really well.<br />-Parvin's twin brother was lovable, except for a few times when he was annoyingly secretive.<br />-A certain man with a fedora was verrrrry hateable.<br />-Jude--I have conflicting feelings about this guy even now. At times I hated him too, at other times I adored him. He was flawed, temperamental, but he had his reasons. So my undecided opinion is not a bad thing! Just an observation!<br />-Hawke--okay, him I like. He had some moments that made me unsure as well, but in other ways he reminded me of the beloved Remko from Rachelle Dekker's Seer trilogy, minus the stutter. I want more Hawke in the next two instalments!<br />-Willow was precious.<br />-One minor character had a strong Ecclesiastes ("everything is useless!") vibe going on, which was intriguing.<br />-The Albinos were despicable and strange and yet some of them had redeeming qualities.<br /><br />I don't even know how to sum up my thoughts on this book! <b>I've been thinking about it for weeks since finishing it</b>. It brought me close to tears. It resonated with me powerfully. The emotions were palpable, the writing was excellent, and the worldbuilding was fleshed out wonderfully. Low cities and high cities, a humongous wall, tightropes, wilderness, a train, the Dregs, emotigraphs, super cool suits: all of it shone through the pages brilliantly. <b>Nadine writes with truckloads of heart, and consequently, mine was broken in a beautiful way.</b><br /><br />Can't wait to read the next two! Five stars!<br /><br /><br /><b>ORIGINAL REVIEW:</b><br />My heart is all over the floor right now. Review to come when I pick up the pieces!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1646887341081009973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1495101524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4591611825089567787">This is the Christian sic-fi version of the Hunger Games. <br/>WOW!<br/><br/>I was exhausted by the end with all that Parvin had gone through. That girl made up for the lack of life she lived before, let me tell you! <br/><br/>Nadine did such a great job with building this new world with: memorable, heartwarming, sweet, interesting and slightly creep characters that seem to stick with you. <br/>I love her play on lemons. Such a unique way for readers to associate to a character. I really thought I was smelling lemons at one </span>
  <span id="freeText4591611825089567787" style="display:none">This is the Christian sic-fi version of the Hunger Games. <br />WOW!<br /><br />I was exhausted by the end with all that Parvin had gone through. That girl made up for the lack of life she lived before, let me tell you! <br /><br />Nadine did such a great job with building this new world with: memorable, heartwarming, sweet, interesting and slightly creep characters that seem to stick with you. <br />I love her play on lemons. Such a unique way for readers to associate to a character. I really thought I was smelling lemons at one point! Also, the fedora helped too! <br />Her creative way to explain a biography was so cool. I mean, who wouldn't want to feel someones emotions at certain points in time? Isn't that why we read oftentimes, to relate? I mean, that part of her book was brilliant! <br /><br />The idea of Shalom was different for me, but not quite a negative. It was the main theme that seemed to drive Parvin on through her path of finding her meaning. It brings her closer to knowing who God is and having a relationship with Him, which I LOVED!!! But, at times, it almost felt like an identity on its own which was a slight confusion for me throughout the book. <br /><br />Still can't wait to continue this series and see where her adventure leads :D <br /><br />13+<br />Recommended as a YA Christian Dystopian Fiction Novel</span>

<div id="review_1486513739" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1486513739" />
    <a title="gabi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40447521-gabi"><img alt="gabi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597861508p2/40447521.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1486513739?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="gabi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="gabi" href="/user/show/40447521-gabi">gabi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40447521-gabi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1486513739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5780193239209893239">Wow. Just wow. I was worried about not liking this after seeing everyone love it. But I shouldn’t have worried. I loved it!<br/><br/>In Parvin Blackwater’s world everyone has a Clock. On that Clock the Numbers tell how long you have to live. Parvin has a year left to live. She wamts to do something meaningful. She wants to be remembered. She begins to think she is doing something right, when she is discovered to be sharing a Clock with her twin brother. As punishment she is thrown through the Wall that di</span>
  <span id="freeText5780193239209893239" style="display:none">Wow. Just wow. I was worried about not liking this after seeing everyone love it. But I shouldn’t have worried. I loved it!<br /><br />In Parvin Blackwater’s world everyone has a Clock. On that Clock the Numbers tell how long you have to live. Parvin has a year left to live. She wamts to do something meaningful. She wants to be remembered. She begins to think she is doing something right, when she is discovered to be sharing a Clock with her twin brother. As punishment she is thrown through the Wall that divides the world in half. On the other side she may find something that can save her people, if she has the time to tell them.<br /><br />Usually when I love a book, it is mainly that characters that I love. It wasn’t exactly the case for this one. I loved all aspects of this book! I only liked Parvin at the beginning, but as I read more she grew on me and now I love her. She seemed very normal, and I liked that. She had a temper, which I totally relate to, but she also had an inner strength which grew as the story went on. There were moments when she was whiny, but I thought it realistic (Aren’t we all whiny at times?). I fell much more easily in love with many of the side characters. Reid was an awesome brother. He was humorous and fun, but was serious about protecting his family. I want to learn more about him! Solomon Hawke was amazing. I loved him from the moment I saw him. He was such a gentleman. He was quiet, but his presence held authority. He was trying to do the right thing, but he might be on the wrong side. Jude, ah, Jude. He seemed to care about know one but himself, but under that hard shell he was caring and loving. He was protective and aggressive. He was mysterious and had many secrets. Willow was a sweet young girl. Elm was neat. I must see more of him! Skelley Chase was a different and unique “bad guy”. I’m still trying to figure out his motives for what he’s done. I kind of liked him, but then he stepped crossed the line. So now I love and hate him.<br /><br />I haven’t read many Christian dystopians, but this was probably the best one I’ve read. The world building was fantastic and unique. I loved the feel of it. I’m still a bit confused about a few of the strange devices in the world, but I get the gist of it.<br /><br />The writing was great. I really do like first person. It was gripping and I found myself really connecting with Parvin in a short amount of time.<br /><br />The plot was ingenious. There were a few things that felt really coincidental, but overall it was pretty realistic for the story. It was slower paced at the beginning, but it quickly sped up. It became unpredictable, intense, scary, exciting, and terrifying all at the same time! The deaths destroyed me! How could that happen? But I think it helped make the story all the more special. But now I’m scared. How many characters are going to make it through this series? The ending was so messed up! I must have the next one! It can’t leave me hanging like that!<br /><br />I’m recommending this to a bit older teens and up because some of the violence was gruesome and might be scary for younger kids. Totally everyone should read this though! It was exceptionally good and I can’t wait to read more!<br /><br />You can check out this review on my blog too, at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://aheartredeemed.wordpress.com/2016/06/27/book-review-a-time-to-die-out-of-time-series-book-1/">https://aheartredeemed.wordpress.com/...</a> Thanks!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5780193239209893239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1715869209" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1715869209" />
    <a title="m a r y l i z" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56772107-m-a-r-y-l-i-z"><img alt="m a r y l i z" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591561393p2/56772107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1715869209?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="m a r y l i z" class="user" itemprop="url" name="m a r y l i z" href="/user/show/56772107-m-a-r-y-l-i-z">m a r y l i z</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1715869209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3465290638137737523">This is a rather tricky book to review. See, I really liked some aspects of the book, but...I didn't totally <i>love</i> it. <br/><br/>I've come to the conclusion that dystopian is not my genre. It's just not. I've tried several different dystopians, but interestingly enough, they all earn about the same rating. I guess I just can never get into it? Maybe it's too depressing for me, I dunno. :P Though I will say that for a dystopian book, <i>A Time to Die</i> was much less dismal than others. In fact, I would argue tha</span>
  <span id="freeText3465290638137737523" style="display:none">This is a rather tricky book to review. See, I really liked some aspects of the book, but...I didn't totally <i>love</i> it. <br /><br />I've come to the conclusion that dystopian is not my genre. It's just not. I've tried several different dystopians, but interestingly enough, they all earn about the same rating. I guess I just can never get into it? Maybe it's too depressing for me, I dunno. :P Though I will say that for a dystopian book, <i>A Time to Die</i> was much less dismal than others. In fact, I would argue that it actually focuses a LOT on hope. Which is awesome! Props to the author for that!<br /><br />ANYWHOZENS. I'm already rambling. *forces train of thought back onto the tracks*<br /><br /><b>// Things I Liked //</b><br /><br />The premise of this book is extremely inventive. Oh, and it's FULL of all kinds of creative things! I don't want to spoil anything but there's a certain person named Wilbur who makes suits...suffice to say, the suits are pretty awesome, and I need them in my life. There are tightropes and cool futuristic technological things (I'm so descriptive :P) and just LOTS OF CREATIVITY. *thumbs up*<br /><br />Another thing I liked about this book was the raw emotion. I absolutely love it when the author makes you <i>feel</i> what the characters feel. It's a sign of an amazing writer. Whenever Parvin was struggling emotionally, physically, or spiritually, I ached for her. This book made me feel. (It also crushed my heart like FIFTY GAZILLION TIMES BUT WHO'S COUNTING &lt;3) And on the topic of characters...<br /><br />I REALLY LIKED THE MAIN CHARACTER. That's always a good thing. Now, she's not my <i>favorite</i> character, per se, but I loved the realism that she has. Honestly, she reminded me a lot of myself in many ways. Physically unable to pull herself up a rope--check. Uses tildes--check. (We're very much alike. XD) <br /><br />I loved following along with Parvin's journey. Seeing how she matured in her faith and gained more purpose was so beautiful. Really, the themes of this book are all great. The importance of using our time wisely, surrendering our life to God, and fighting for what we believe really cuts to the heart, challenging each and every reader who picks up this book. It's always refreshing to see books that stimulate our brains and make us think about important truths.<br /><br />Also...I. NEED. MORE. HAWKE. &lt;3 He is honestly the best. End of story.<br /><br />Okay, now on to my dislikes. :/<br /><br /><b>// Things I Didn't Like //</b><br /><br />This book was written in first person present tense. This is in NO way the fault of the writer--I'm sure there are lots of people who like present tense. However, I am not one of them. I had no idea it was written in that tense before I picked it up. So that was a bit of a bummer. (Although I will admit that I kind of got used to it after a while. It just wasn't my favorite.) I know this may sound like a shallow reason, but I honestly just can't get into a book as much when it's written in a tense I feel is awkward.<br /><br />I also never really liked a lot of the characters. YES, I KNOW I JUST SAID I LIKED PARVIN AND HAWKE. But I reallllllllly didn't like a lot of characters in this book. I waver between loathing/loving Jude. He actually made me kind of want to throw my tablet across the room more than once. XD Honestly, the only two characters I liked a lot were Parvin and Hawke. *shrugs*<br /><br />The action also tended to be...well, nonexistent. They seemed to spend the majority of the book wandering around or arguing. :P I kept waiting for exciting things to happen--and yes, they did sometimes--but I felt like every time the action would get going, it would quickly be squashed by some huge setback. Thankfully, I was invested enough in the plot and main character (and Hawke &lt;3) that I wanted to keep reading. ^_^<br /><br />There was also a certain romance I DID NOT APPROVE OF AT ALL. Nooo thank you.<br /><br />Content wise, this book contains a little bit of violence and such. I maaaay have cringed during some of the scenes. ;) There is also some romance, though the author keeps it all clean. So I would probably recommend this to teens around the age of 13, just for some of the violence. <br /><br />Overall, I <i>did</i> like this book! There just were quite a few things I didn't care for. :/ Hopefully this didn't come off as too scathing a review at the end...eheh. :P I just wanted to be honest about the book since Miss Brandes herself was generous enough to give me a free review copy! (Thanks loads, Nadine! :D) <br /><br /><b>Final Consensus: 3 Stars</b><br /><br />So did I enjoy this book? Yes, I did. Will I be picking up the second book? ABSOLUTELY YES. I'm kind of emotionally invested now. I NEED TO KNOW WHAT ELSE HAPPENS. *grabby hands*<br /><br />(Read my <a href="http://sunshineandscribblings.blogspot.com/2016/09/book-review-time-to-die-nadine-brandes.html" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a> on my blog. ^_^)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3465290638137737523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5989586247182626021">I. MUST. READ. THE. NEXT. BOOK. Seriously though. After having this series highly recommended to me by several friends, I got the first book as a Christmas a present from my grandparents. After the holiday business and starting college business, I finally had a couple days of solid reading and finished it. Finished it with heart beating about five times as rapidly as it should. <br/>The whole idea of lives being run by clocks and all manner of electronic chips you could put in your mind was fascinati</span>
  <span id="freeText5989586247182626021" style="display:none">I. MUST. READ. THE. NEXT. BOOK. Seriously though. After having this series highly recommended to me by several friends, I got the first book as a Christmas a present from my grandparents. After the holiday business and starting college business, I finally had a couple days of solid reading and finished it. Finished it with heart beating about five times as rapidly as it should. <br />The whole idea of lives being run by clocks and all manner of electronic chips you could put in your mind was fascinating. And I enjoyed the variety of characters and settings the author wove throughout the book. A fabulous and intense read with lots of feels. I think it'll take a couple days for me to relax again after all that tension. <br />So if it's a fabulous book, why only four stars? Well, two reasons: first, I found myself frustrated with Parvin for most of the story and hard to relate to everything I think I was supposed relate to. The second reason, I thought the cliff-hanger endings of the chapters were overused. They lost their effect halfway through the book. If not sooner.<br /><br />Also, the smell of lemons WILL NEVER BE THE SAME. </span>

<div id="review_1495279840" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1495279840" />
    <a title="Serethiel ☽ ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50374139-serethiel"><img alt="Serethiel ☽ ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548185365p2/50374139.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1495279840?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Serethiel ☽ ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Serethiel ☽ ✨" href="/user/show/50374139-serethiel">Serethiel ☽ ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer5979421380133314122">I've seen this book hyped up since I joined Goodreads, and ended up buying the whole series in paperback with some Christmas money. I read this first one in a couple of days. <br/><br/>And sheesh, was the hype worth it. <br/><br/>LIKES:<br/>-This is Christian fiction that is NOT AFRAID to get real. And dark. And I love that. Life in the Christian world is not all fun and games, and it's a little weird to go from this to Mitford....but I still love them both. <3 And the fact that the darkness is not GLORIFIED but is in t</span>
  <span id="freeText5979421380133314122" style="display:none">I've seen this book hyped up since I joined Goodreads, and ended up buying the whole series in paperback with some Christmas money. I read this first one in a couple of days. <br /><br />And sheesh, was the hype worth it. <br /><br />LIKES:<br />-This is Christian fiction that is NOT AFRAID to get real. And dark. And I love that. Life in the Christian world is not all fun and games, and it's a little weird to go from this to Mitford....but I still love them both. &lt;3 And the fact that the darkness is not GLORIFIED but is in there to depict that this is a fallen world.... *all the heart eyes*<br />-PARVIN. Her internal journeys spoke to me so so so much. I mean, she starts out so selfish and caring only about herself, wondering if her family even loves her, angry at herself for wasting her life up to this point....but her character arc is immense throughout this story and I adore it. &lt;3<br />-Willow. Poor sweet little Willow. &lt;3 And Ash! I really liked Ash!<br />-Jude. As an individual, however. I'll talk a little bit (in spoilers) about what I DIDN'T like about him in the next section. For now, suffice it to say: That personality! And that ending!<br />-All the locations and steampunky stuff! Wilber's suits! Wilber himself! Ivanhoe which was just PERFECT and I adore it! (Air/wind is my element, so the idea of a city where everything is wide open and tightropes and all of that...*squeals*) <br />-The messages of truth that were so prevalent throughout were just sort of YES<br />-I absolutely loved Skelley Chase (both as a character and...ya know...after the plot twist.)<br />-Reid! <br />-HAAAAAAWWWWWWKKKKKEEEEEEEEEEEE forever <br />-Parvin's parents are great! <br /><br />DISLIKES<br />-Elm. I'm sorry, guys, I just do not like him. :P<br />-Jude. So, I get that he has anger management issues and all that, but <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It is never okay to hit a woman. Ever. I'm sorry, but....I just couldn't love him after that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br />-I mentioned above that I like the grittiness of this book, but a couple of times, it got to be just a little TOO dark. One scene in particular: WELL MY GOODNESS. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[You all know the one...when Jude wants her to try to cut out his tracker... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> For the most part it didn't bother me. But then things got weird. XD<br /><br />Overall? Four stars to this one, and I love the rest of the series! Definitely not for everyone, but if you're looking for gritty Christian fiction that really doesn't shy away from the darkness in the world but still shines God's light through, I would ABSOLUTELY recommend this book. &lt;3 <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16828811119637291796">I really enjoyed this book. I originally had this at five stars, but decided to take away a star after I really got down to the core of the book. Let me give the rundown:<br/><br/>-Language: a few ugly words like 'idiot', etc. <br/>-Violence: a LOT to be on the look out for. Fighting, guns, etc. Nothing so descriptive I couldn't read it, but I would caution readers under the age of 12-13. <br/>-Blood/Gore: a good bit in this category also. Several characters get limbs cut off (semi-detailed) and a lot of detail abo</span>
  <span id="freeText16828811119637291796" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book. I originally had this at five stars, but decided to take away a star after I really got down to the core of the book. Let me give the rundown:<br /><br />-Language: a few ugly words like 'idiot', etc. <br />-Violence: a LOT to be on the look out for. Fighting, guns, etc. Nothing so descriptive I couldn't read it, but I would caution readers under the age of 12-13. <br />-Blood/Gore: a good bit in this category also. Several characters get limbs cut off (semi-detailed) and a lot of detail about injuries and illness. <br />-Romance: attraction between Parvin and a boy (like I'll ever tell who) , hand holding/touching, a cheek kiss [overall, not much, but what was there was sweet!)<br /><br />I LOVED this. Parvin's journey has been keeping me clueless until the end of the book! (and I'm still left hanging because there are two more books in the trilogy!!!)<br /><br />What I thought about the characters:<br /><br />-Parvin:<br />WHAT A CHARACTER!! wow. After she *mild spoiler* lost her arm, I had a deeper respect for her. Her entire journey so far has been really intriguing. I especially liked her messages with Hawke. <br />-Hawke: <br />Um, can I please have MORE of Hawke? He was SO sweet and caring about Parvin! In the end when they finally saw each other, he was still holding her. Then the book ended. (Nadine, please stop torturing me!) I've already read reviews for the next book so I know he's coming back! #teamHawke<br />-Jude: <br />I must confess that I have had mixed feelings about Jude. He was sent to help Parvin, but he was hiding a lot of things and so I just didn't really trust him for a while. I really felt for him though (especially after the way things turned out. WOW! Gut wrenching for sure). <br />-Reid:<br />The pErFeCt brother for sure. However, I didn't care for Reid so much because of how he left Parvin. (Which isn't really a spoiler people)<br />-Willow:<br />what a sweet girl! and an albino too? AWESOME! Looking forward to reading more of her.<br /><br />Overall, my only regret is that I don't have the next two books! I rated it four stars because of the amount of violence and blood. <br /><br />Would recommend to ages 13+ and to lovers of a dystopian adventure with hints of romance. :)<br /><br />Well done, Mrs. Brandes!!!</span>

<div id="review_1354393316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1354393316" />
    <a title="Ashley Bogner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43202587-ashley-bogner"><img alt="Ashley Bogner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549942031p2/43202587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1354393316?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Bogner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Bogner" href="/user/show/43202587-ashley-bogner">Ashley Bogner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43202587-ashley-bogner?shelf=books-i-read-in-2016">books-i-read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43202587-ashley-bogner?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43202587-ashley-bogner?shelf=most-original-storylines">most-original-storylines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1354393316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11015556152138711943">Parvin Blackwater lives in a world where everyone knows the day they will die. With only one year left on her Clock, Parvin realizes she hasn't done anything meaningful. She tries to find a purpose, which results in her being exiled from her home and sent to the world beyond the Wall. What will she find there? Will she survive?<br/><br/>I thought <i> A Time to Die </i> was very thought-provoking and asks some tough questions. How would we live if we knew the day we would die? Do we put God's plan above our own? </span>
  <span id="freeText11015556152138711943" style="display:none">Parvin Blackwater lives in a world where everyone knows the day they will die. With only one year left on her Clock, Parvin realizes she hasn't done anything meaningful. She tries to find a purpose, which results in her being exiled from her home and sent to the world beyond the Wall. What will she find there? Will she survive?<br /><br />I thought <i> A Time to Die </i> was very thought-provoking and asks some tough questions. How would we live if we knew the day we would die? Do we put God's plan above our own? Do we trust Him in all circumstances? This book leaves readers with a lot to think about.<br /><br />Also, I loved the first-person, present-tense narrative. I felt like I was always in Parvin’s head and saw her grow throughout the story.<br /><br />The characters are interesting, and Nadine Brandes does a great job with conveying emotions. Actually, her writing is great. Period. There were times where I couldn't believe this was a debut novel. So much depth! <br /><br />There were quite a few twists that were "I didn't see that coming" moments. <i> A Time to Die </i> is very fast-paced, and I found myself constantly thinking "just one more chapter...", but one chapter would soon turn into five. The story is unique and stands out among the dozens of dystopian novels out there.<br /><br />My one complaint would be that some parts of the book were a little too gory for me (characters lose limbs, a birth scene, several scenes involving characters having to stitch up their own wounds, etc). The book, overall, felt dark and it seemed like nothing could ever go right for Parvin. But it also had a sense of hope that’s missing from a lot of other dystopian novels. And that CLIFFHANGER!!!!!!!!!! <br /><br />No profanity, and sexual content is mild. <br /><br /><i> A Time to Die </i> was definitely interesting, and Nadine Brandes knows how to tug at her readers' emotions. Parts of the book were hard for me to stomach (but I'm pretty squeamish!). Overall, I loved the themes and it was definitely a book I couldn't put down.<br /><br />The sequel, <i> A Time to Speak </i>, is very high on my to-read list!<br /><br />Oh, yes, and I love the cover. ;)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11015556152138711943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sierra Faith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30959621-sierra-faith"><img alt="Sierra Faith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418396968p2/30959621.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1111834797?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sierra Faith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sierra Faith" href="/user/show/30959621-sierra-faith">Sierra Faith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30959621-sierra-faith?shelf=books-to-read-in-2015">books-to-read-in-2015</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1111834797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7445600124984089024">A Time to Die<br/><br/>Genre: Christian, Dystopian.<br/><br/>Favorite Quote: “You shouldn’t be placing hope in our lives, Parvin. That’s my point. I don’t know the answers of the future, but your confidence and hope need to be in God.” <br/><br/>Age Range: 14+ (See end of review)<br/><br/>POV: First person, Parvin.<br/><br/>Stars: 4/5<br/><br/>The whole idea for this book was unique; I found it very interesting. The setting of A Time to Die is a Dystopian world where everyone knows the day they die, for Parvin that day is soon.<br/><br/>I fell in love with Parvin,</span>
  <span id="freeText7445600124984089024" style="display:none">A Time to Die<br /><br />Genre: Christian, Dystopian.<br /><br />Favorite Quote: “You shouldn’t be placing hope in our lives, Parvin. That’s my point. I don’t know the answers of the future, but your confidence and hope need to be in God.” <br /><br />Age Range: 14+ (See end of review)<br /><br />POV: First person, Parvin.<br /><br />Stars: 4/5<br /><br />The whole idea for this book was unique; I found it very interesting. The setting of A Time to Die is a Dystopian world where everyone knows the day they die, for Parvin that day is soon.<br /><br />I fell in love with Parvin, the main character. At first I thought her whiny and she grated on my nerves, but it didn't take long to change my mind! I loved Parvin's growing faith throughout the book. This story has made me ponder on my life. If I was to die tomorrow, would I have wasted my life on worthless things? This whole book just made me think.<br /><br /><br />With this being a fictional setting I felt like some aspects of the story could have been explained better. I couldn't picture some of the buildings that Parvin visited. There were also a couple of devices I was very confused as to how they worked or what they looked like (the emotigraph, for example). I would have appreciated a little more information.<br /><br /><br />For this being Nadine's debut novel she did an AMAZING job. I am super excited for her second book A Time to Speak. It's releasing sometime this fall, which is too far away if you ask me.<br /><br /><br />I would caution sensitive people due to a birth scene and several detailed "surgery" scenes.<br /><br /><br />Overall: I loved this book and I have plans to re-read it this summer! <br /><br /><br />(Original review found on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://26countlesspossibilities.wordpress.com/2015/06/19/review-a-time-to-die/">https://26countlesspossibilities.word...</a>)</span>
